< Review>
Ding Tea in Pomona is a very pleasant place to shop for tea. The location is clean. Their menu is diverse. The staff greeted me upon entering and waited patiently for me to choose my drinks. My wait time was reasonable and my drinks were done right. The tea temperature was perfect and the boba tasted fresh. I recommend this location and will take family and friends for delicious drinks.</Review>

< review>
Super divey and hipster bar! Was in town visiting family and my cousin suggested this place. It's super casual and they have a really fun shuffleboard table! We ordered some beers and cocktails, but the best part were the free pretzels! How many bars offer free ANYTHING  (besides water)?! Bartenders are super chill and not obnoxious at all. We also ordered the dolma as a snack and they were delicious. The music was mostly throwbacks which are really fun to sing along to when you're buzzing! Overall, I'm a fan and I'm glad that we came here.< /review>

Wow! So glad my husband surprised me with a couples massage for my birthday. This spa is absolutely gorgeous. Really amazing decor and customer service. It definitely has the ‚Äòwow‚Äô factor. Great place to host a party! The robes and slippers are wonderful. The robe is super soft on the inside with a satiny type fabric on the outside-my favorite.

The couples massage room was spacious and cozy. We didn‚Äôt want to leave. I had a relaxing massage with Jasmine. My husband had a deep tissue/sports medicine style massage with LaJuan. He said that the massage was very intense, but he felt so much better afterwards and would go back. So if you like more pressure/intensity, ask for LaJuan. Jasmine is definitely a better therapist if you want something that makes you feel relaxed and drowsy.

The waiting rooms were beautiful. We received complimentary champagne and chocolate. They also had tea, water, fruit, and gingerbread cookies!

Only negative would be the women‚Äôs lounge. It is small with only two sinks to get ready. And it gets super hot with the steam room and hair dryers. It was 78 degrees and I was super warm.

Overall, loved this spa. Planning on going with my mom and one of my friends in the future! Great value, great experience.</review>

<Rating>3</Rating><Response>None<//Response><user>103960026898958587973< /user>< Review>
This review in no way reflects my massage therapist. She was great, professional, and kind. Unfortunately, I am bad with remembering names, so she will go down as a 5 Star unsung hero....

The 3 star is for the spa itself. While everything was fine and harmonious and all that, i just didn't love this spa. I guess I am spoiled with my first spa experience being the Four Seasons in Westlake Village.  Kelly's Spa is located in the historic Mission Inn, in downtown Riverside.  The entrance to the spa was actually really pleasant, i think they have some type of scent generator outside haha.

Once in, the check in area is a little small, but very peaceful, and loaded with merch. The staff is super friendly. My real  gripes with this place are:
The size. It is small and you just don't feel free.
Not a fan of the co-ed waiting area.
The steam room was luke warm
The showers are small and there are only 2
The positives are the price. While it is small, there are full amenities. Even with my 25 minute massage i was offered champagne. The staff is

< Review>
Valley Crossfit
PROS: Lots of time options for classes, specialty classes, big and spacious with professional, well maintained equipment, spring floor, Big parking lot, community atmosphere, knowledgeable and friendly staff

CONS: Some classes can get full, can become addicting.

At the End Of January 2017, I had a Facebook ad show up about a  six week fitness challenge offered by Valley Crossfit (VCF) I work a 9-5 behind a computer screen and really wanted to make a positive
change .

Having never tried Crossfit, I was a worried about feeling like a deuce walking into a gym, somewhere I never go. I signed up.  From the start the staff and coaches made me feel like I was part of the team and never judgemental. it was tough but fun and challenges you to become a better version of yourself.

The coaches will scale workouts according to your ability and keep you motivated. Communication via the Facebook group really helps you stay connected, ask questions, get answers and gives the community feeling validity. I signed up for a regular membership after finishing the challenge and I couldn't be happier.

All of the same feelings apply and are not exclusive to the six week challenge.  Valley Crossfit has been the cornerstone of Motivation and Positive Change.

Highly recommended for anyone looking for a place to get in shape in a welcoming environment without judgment and an attentive professional staff.
See ya there soon, come say hi.</Review>

Unfortunately my experience here was subpar. The 2 stars is for the facility only: there's no denying that they have that down. This is not my 1st time with crossfit but I'm not drinking the CF kool aid (fulltime) either. I attended VCF 3x/wk for a couple of months and there was no sense of direction as far as programming was concerned: most coaches were making things up as they went along. And if you switched coaches during the week, their 'freestyle/imaginary programming' is completely different from the previous coach. The owner (Mike) is very impatient, sarcastic and constantly makes demeaning jokes towards students. I understand the need to be humorous during class, but not at the expense of a person in attendance. Being the first CF gym in the valley doesn't always make it the best place to try crossfit. So yeah, keep looking...<//text>

This is a gym for obsessed crossfit workout fanatics who like to be yelled at and made to feel like garbage while trying to get in better shape.  Not good for an average person looking for a basic workout.  I am someone who enjoys fitness and tries to do what I can to stay in shape... this place is not for me.  The main guy Mike (who was running the class the day I went) was a total d-bag.  He's mean, snarky, condescending and has a huge attitude.  And that attitude seems to have permeated to the regulars in the gym because they all basically had the same attitude.  Makes sense since the gym aims to create a psyco-bootcamp lifestyle - and a drill sergeant traditionally sets the tone for those under him.

If you are a professional crossfit health nut, this is probably the right place to be.  If you're someone just trying to get in better shape... I would go elsewhere.  There are a few other new style gyms in the area that I hear give a much more positive experience.   Everyone takes themselves way too seriously here.  It's just a gym!  I guess I will have to keep looking for another way to keep my workouts fun.</text>

<review>From a Vendor point of view: Wednesday's space fee is way overpriced @ $25. Hardly any customers show up. Vendors are allowed to sell fake name brands such as Michael Kors, Adidas, Nike Pink as well as others and none of the staff says anything. This makes it really hard on the vendors who go out and by the real items and try to complete reselling against the fakes. Not Right and its illegal. The management of the Madera flea market should consider advertising more or doing something to draw more customers in and make it a better experience for all. It's time to stop raking in the money and telling all the vendors what they can't do and maybe try telling the vendors what you have done for them since they're the only reason that the entire flea market is open. Everybody steps on the little guy until he becomes your boss. On a positive note the food is great the vegetables look fabulous and most of the vendors are pretty nice, even most of the staff seem to have a real positive attitude.

I tell one, I tell all, come support the vendors at all the flea markets. Come and have a great time. Come and eat some delicious food. Take home some very unique and fabulous items. But remember the vendors work hard to pick, front the cash and buy this stuff for you. They can't sell it at a cheaper price than they paid, so please be considerate in your negotiations and don't insult a vendor buy offering half the price,  that they are asking. If you can't come somewhat close to their asking price  just being nice say thank you and move on. You have so many choices  that you don't have to insult the vendor, just a little word of advice.< /review>< Pics>
